  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6faa2fbb-bc2c-4ca1-b6bd-2f91a78ecb3a'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer12502495305623316354">Each sunrise seems to bring fresh reasons for fear.<br/><br/>They're talking layoffs at work, slowdowns in the economy, flare-ups in the Middle East, turnovers at headquarters, downturns in the housing market, upswings in global warming.   <span id="freeText12502495305623316354" style="display:none">Each sunrise seems to bring fresh reasons for fear.<br /><br />They're talking layoffs at work, slowdowns in the economy, flare-ups in the Middle East, turnovers at headquarters, downturns in the housing market, upswings in global warming. The plague of our day, terrorism, begins with the word "terror." Fear, it seems, has taken up a hundred-year lease on the building next door and set up shop. Oversized and rude, fear herds us into a prison of unlocked doors. Wouldn't it be great to walk out?<br /><br />Imagine your life, wholly untouched by angst. What if faith, not fear, was your default reaction to threats? If you could hover a fear magnet over your heart and extract every last shaving of dread, insecurity, or doubt, what would remain? Envision a day, just one day, where you could trust more and fear less.<br /><br />Can you imagine your life without fear?</span>

<div id="review_140069963" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/140069963" />
    <a title="Fylvia Kline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4793950-fylvia-kline"><img alt="Fylvia Kline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321721635p2/4793950.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/140069963?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fylvia Kline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fylvia Kline" href="/user/show/4793950-fylvia-kline">Fylvia Kline</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8127238-fearless">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer140069963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4186149752043263320">Fearless arrived in the mail at 2 pm today. Four hours, several snacks and a few pillow fluffings later, I’ve come to the last page. And I feel affirmed of my normalcy, of my humaness. I also feel encouraged about tomorrow and what it could bring. The book has challenged me to take fear on with the power of God’s presence<br/><br/>If you are a Christian feeling the brunt of life–death, recession, disappointment, whatever–and are afraid, this is a must-read, an investment to a better future. Of course, it </span>
  <span id="freeText4186149752043263320" style="display:none">Fearless arrived in the mail at 2 pm today. Four hours, several snacks and a few pillow fluffings later, I’ve come to the last page. And I feel affirmed of my normalcy, of my humaness. I also feel encouraged about tomorrow and what it could bring. The book has challenged me to take fear on with the power of God’s presence<br /><br />If you are a Christian feeling the brunt of life–death, recession, disappointment, whatever–and are afraid, this is a must-read, an investment to a better future. Of course, it doesn’t magically take the bad stuff away or blind you to harsh realities. But it does help change your attitude and perspective.The overall theme of the book is that in order to live in contentment and peace–in spite of the fearful situations in life–you need to believe that God is in control and you need to let God be in control.<br /><br />Fears are real and creep into all our lives.”Yet left unchecked, they metastasize into obsessions” (p.80). This does not mean that you should not be proactive or make calculated decisions. Lacado points out that there is a fine line between prudence and paranoia–Use judgment and common sense in practical and spiritual choices, but don’t get drowned while contemplating on all the things that could go wrong.<br /><br />With his usual mastery of storytelling, Lucado weaves lives of people into practical lessons of coping with fear. His honest exposition of the topic includes an examination of his own fears. I found the book very relevant it connects the subject with present time–people gripped in difficult economic situations. The book makes the exorcism of fear a personal journey and places a caring Savior right in the middle of all of our worries.<br /><br />My favorite part of the book was early on in the book –Lucado describes Jesus sleeping on the boat during a storm and the disciples interpreting his sound sleep as a Master who did not care. From this, the author draws two points crucial to surviving fear: 1) Fear can unravel our belief in God’s goodness; 2) Being a Christian does not exclude tough, scary times. Throughout the book, he comes back to these two points in different ways. The bottom line is you can curl up and give up or you can live unafraid, knowing that “if it hasn’t gotten better, it’s not the end.”<br /><br />In Lucado’s eloquent words: ” Getting on board with Christ can mean getting soaked with Christ.”<br /><br />(Note: I received this book free from Thomas Nelson Publishers as part of their BookSneeze.com  book review bloggers program. I was not required to write a positive review. The opinions I have expressed are my own. I am disclosing this in accordance with the Federal Trade Commission’s 16 CFR, Part 255)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4186149752043263320" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/155742657" />
    <a title="Seth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5155017-seth"><img alt="Seth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416803016p2/5155017.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/155742657?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Seth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Seth" href="/user/show/5155017-seth">Seth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5155017-seth?shelf=christianity">christianity</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer155742657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16423584607102937795">I had never read a Max Lucado book before Fearless. Not that I was unfamiliar with his name; it’s hard to recall a Christian home I entered during childhood that didn’t have at least one of his books on a shelf. So I had high expectations for the quality of spiritual depth and practical insight I hoped to encounter while reading this one. Unfortunately, I came away disappointed.<br/><br/>I suppose the book succeeds at its goal—to discuss humanity’s relationship with fear in all aspects of our lives and in</span>
  <span id="freeText16423584607102937795" style="display:none">I had never read a Max Lucado book before Fearless. Not that I was unfamiliar with his name; it’s hard to recall a Christian home I entered during childhood that didn’t have at least one of his books on a shelf. So I had high expectations for the quality of spiritual depth and practical insight I hoped to encounter while reading this one. Unfortunately, I came away disappointed.<br /><br />I suppose the book succeeds at its goal—to discuss humanity’s relationship with fear in all aspects of our lives and in a myriad manifestations, and to explain and exhort the power of the Gospel to understand, dispel and defeat it. But the presentation was simply not my cup of tea. It read like Chicken Soup for the Christian Soul, with the obligatory inspirational stories and pithy quotes—but marinaded in Bible verses. While theological, Fearless felt like a surface level self-help tome rather than a meaty and intellectually challenging work of profundity. Also, the brazen commercialization of assorted and related products advertised in the back of the book—which, admittedly, likely have more to do with the publisher than the author—left a sour taste in my mouth and served to remind me why I avoid Christian bookstores at all cost.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16423584607102937795" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_146161767" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/146161767" />
    <a title="John" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4929332-john"><img alt="John" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1296926307p2/4929332.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/146161767?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John" href="/user/show/4929332-john">John</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer146161767" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1299745493555832998"><br/>Fear. <br/><br/>Everyone knows that name. <br/><br/>You can see it on the face of a startled infant; you can see it in the eyes of a dying man. Fear is one of the inescapable consequences of being human. <br/><br/>Or is it? <br/><br/>Is it possible to live without fear? <br/><br/>Max Lucado says we can fight fear, and learn to live without its life-draining presence, as we learn to trust in Christ. <br/><br/>His newest book, Fearless, examines fear and how we can combat it. Starting with the nature of fear, he deals chapter by chapter with a wide variety</span>
  <span id="freeText1299745493555832998" style="display:none"><br />Fear. <br /><br />Everyone knows that name. <br /><br />You can see it on the face of a startled infant; you can see it in the eyes of a dying man. Fear is one of the inescapable consequences of being human. <br /><br />Or is it? <br /><br />Is it possible to live without fear? <br /><br />Max Lucado says we can fight fear, and learn to live without its life-draining presence, as we learn to trust in Christ. <br /><br />His newest book, Fearless, examines fear and how we can combat it. Starting with the nature of fear, he deals chapter by chapter with a wide variety of fears we commonly face, including significance, parenting, violence, and our relationship with God. In his trademark style of wisdom, compassion, &amp; hope, Maxwell points us beyond our fears to Christ: <br /><br />"It's not the absence of storms that sets us apart. It's whom we discover in the storm: an unstirred Christ... Whether or not storms come, we cannot choose. But where we stare during a storm, that we can. ... Do whatever it takes to keep your gaze on Jesus..." <br /><br />In the back of the book is an excellent study guide that digs deeper into each chapter. Each chapter of the guide has space for journaling "examining fear" (reflecting on key ideas from the chapter), "exposing fear" (reflecting on key Bible verses), and "battling fear" (practical steps of faith). <br /><br />All of us have to face fear. Lucado reminds us that we do not have to face it alone. A good book to read and share.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1299745493555832998" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_70501392" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/70501392" />
    <a title="Chris Hyde" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/775863-chris-hyde"><img alt="Chris Hyde" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580404819p2/775863.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/70501392?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris Hyde" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris Hyde" href="/user/show/775863-chris-hyde">Chris Hyde</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer70501392" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12882845105097942703">For many years, I read each of Max Lucado’s books as they came out. After all, Max Lucado is one of the most widely-read Christian authors of our time. I loved his books. But after a while, I have to be honest, I got bored of his books. They just seemed like they were “same old, same old”. So I went for a long time without reading his newer releases. But then came the opportunity to read an advance copy of his latest book, “Fearless”. I thought, “OK…I’ll try one of his books again.”<br/><br/>“We are peppe</span>
  <span id="freeText12882845105097942703" style="display:none">For many years, I read each of Max Lucado’s books as they came out. After all, Max Lucado is one of the most widely-read Christian authors of our time. I loved his books. But after a while, I have to be honest, I got bored of his books. They just seemed like they were “same old, same old”. So I went for a long time without reading his newer releases. But then came the opportunity to read an advance copy of his latest book, “Fearless”. I thought, “OK…I’ll try one of his books again.”<br /><br />“We are peppered with bad news. Global warming, asteroid attack, SARS, genocide, wars, earthquakes, tsunamis, AIDS…does it ever stop? The bad news is taking its toll. We are the most worried culture that has ever lived. For the first time since the end of the Second World War, parents expect that life for the next generation will be worse than it was for them.” (page 177)<br /><br />“Fearless” has got to be the best book Lucado has written in years! While I am not a person who deals with fears, I read this book with great interest because I have several people in my life who do wrestle with fears. Chapter by chapter, Lucado addresses specific fears that people may face: Fear of Disappointing God, Fear of Not Protecting Your Kids, Fear of Violence, Fear of Death, Fear of What’s Next, Fear That God is Not Real, and many others. In each chapter, Lucado provides stories, Biblical Scriptures, and an explanation of how we can conquer that specific fear. As I read the book, I found myself getting more and more excited about how this book could make a difference in the lives of people who are hindered by their fears.<br /><br />“Fearless” is being released TODAY! If you are a fan of Max Lucado or are someone who recognizes that fear affects your life, I highly recommend this book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12882845105097942703" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1311017471" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1311017471" />
    <a title="Bex Montgomery" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2404020-bex-montgomery"><img alt="Bex Montgomery" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500699276p2/2404020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1311017471?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bex Montgomery" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bex Montgomery" href="/user/show/2404020-bex-montgomery">Bex Montgomery</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2404020-bex-montgomery?shelf=aurelia-reviews">aurelia-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1311017471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17600255023809212120"><b>About <i>Fearless</i>:</b><br/>Seeking to calm a world increasingly plagued by fear and anxiety, Max Lucado tackles the subject of fear with this inspirational title, identifying common fears of the day, and offering spiritual advice for overcoming our fears.<br/><br/><b>The Review:</b><br/>As someone who has suffered from anxiety and fear most of my life, I often seek out books on the subject. This was one that I had acquired years ago for review, and had slipped through the cracks. I’m not a religious person, though there was a ti</span>
  <span id="freeText17600255023809212120" style="display:none"><b>About <i>Fearless</i>:</b><br>Seeking to calm a world increasingly plagued by fear and anxiety, Max Lucado tackles the subject of fear with this inspirational title, identifying common fears of the day, and offering spiritual advice for overcoming our fears.<br><br><b>The Review:</b><br>As someone who has suffered from anxiety and fear most of my life, I often seek out books on the subject. This was one that I had acquired years ago for review, and had slipped through the cracks. I’m not a religious person, though there was a time in my life that I was, and I still have a great respect for the wisdom that can come from many of the world’s religions. So knowing that this title came from a Christian publisher did not give me too much pause. I figured I would still find some tips in it that I would find beneficial.<br><br>I was greatly disappointed. It was set up like this: Each chapter highlighted a common fear. Lucado then illustrated the fear with stories either from his own life or from the lives of others, went on to tie it to a bible story, and then to the scriptures that had Christ saying in one form or another “Don’t Fear” “God will Provide.”<br><br>Next Chapter? Repeat. Ad Nauseum.<br><br>At one point on his “Don’t Worry Be Happy” campaign he pulls out this gem...<br><br><blockquote>Like a good shepherd, he will not let us go unclothed or unfed. “I have never seen the godly abandoned or their children begging for bread” (Ps. 37:25 nlt).</blockquote><br><br>…And I wanted to slam the book against a wall and scream at the man living in his high house on a hill, because I HAVE. And this is no longer a book about overcoming fear, it is about deluding yourself into giving all your fears away to someone else so you don’t have to deal with them. It’s the worst kind of avoidance.<br><br>It’s not that I don’t appreciate the concept of Faith and admire Christians for practicing it. It’s just that I admire the adage that “Faith without works is dead” more. And Lucado’s book is sorely lacking in the works department.<br><br>He does not provide any strategies or methods for actually DEALING with fear or anxiety other than turning to Jesus. Not only is this not an attractive option for everyone, it’s not a real answer. It’s not doing the work to enact any real change.<br><br>Another gem of a quote from the book was this one:<br><br><blockquote>“Everything will work out in the end, if it’s not working out, it’s not the end”</blockquote><br><br>Helpful right? What does that even mean?<br><br><b>The Wrap Up</b><br>Bottom line. If you are deeply Christian, and a fan of Lucado’s vast body of work you may find comfort in his brand of scriptural junk food for the soul, but he excludes anyone else as an audience. And don’t expect to find any real advice. This is not a self-help book and it’s certainly doesn't come close to even pop psychology.<br><br>If you are battling clinical anxiety, phobias or dealing with irrational fears, don’t look to this book for help.<br><br>Here’s what I’d recommend instead:<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8527134.The_Anxiety_and_Phobia_Workbook" title="The Anxiety and Phobia Workbook by Edmund J. Bourne" rel="nofollow noopener">The Anxiety and Phobia Workbook</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/67223.Edmund_J__Bourne" title="Edmund J. Bourne" rel="nofollow noopener">Edmund J. Bourne</a><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/653396.Feel_the_Fear_and_Do_It_Anyway" title="Feel the Fear and Do It Anyway by Susan Jeffers" rel="nofollow noopener">Feel the Fear and Do It Anyway</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4562105.Susan_Jeffers" title="Susan Jeffers" rel="nofollow noopener">Susan Jeffers</a><br><br>And for the spiritually minded, a more practical approach:<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13623836.Fear_Essential_Wisdom_for_Getting_Through_the_Storm" title="Fear Essential Wisdom for Getting Through the Storm by Thích Nhất Hạnh" rel="nofollow noopener">Fear: Essential Wisdom for Getting Through the Storm</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9074.Th_ch_Nh_t_H_nh" title="Thích Nhất Hạnh" rel="nofollow noopener">Thích Nhất Hạnh</a><br><br><b>My Rating:</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434690244i/15253522.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Cover Story: B-</b><br>Basically, I blame the cover for my confidence in the book in the first place. I wanted that happy-go-lucky childhood summer free from fears, and I hoped this book would show me how.<br><br>Review Copy Courtesy of Thomas Nelson/BookLook Bloggers<br><br>This review originally appeared at <a href="http://www.aurelmedia.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Aurelia {Lit}</a> </span>
  <a data-text-id="17600255023809212120" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_474006513" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/474006513" />
    <a title="Bryon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7696135-bryon"><img alt="Bryon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328887954p2/7696135.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/474006513?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bryon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bryon" href="/user/show/7696135-bryon">Bryon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer474006513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7579936715004024493"><br/><br/><br/>0<br/><br/>inShare<br/>"We fear being sued, finishing last, going broke; we fear the mole on the back, the new kid on the block, the sound of the clock as it ticks us closer to the grave," writes Max Lucado in his latest book "Fearless."<br/><br/>Whether rational or irrational, we live in a world and a time in history that startles and alarms us. Author and pastor Max Lucado writes to remind us that this is neither necessary nor productive, but he doesn't chide or ridicule the reader.<br/><br/>You may think you're fearless. But, </span>
  <span id="freeText7579936715004024493" style="display:none"><br /><br /><br />0<br /><br />inShare<br />"We fear being sued, finishing last, going broke; we fear the mole on the back, the new kid on the block, the sound of the clock as it ticks us closer to the grave," writes Max Lucado in his latest book "Fearless."<br /><br />Whether rational or irrational, we live in a world and a time in history that startles and alarms us. Author and pastor Max Lucado writes to remind us that this is neither necessary nor productive, but he doesn't chide or ridicule the reader.<br /><br />You may think you're fearless. But, no doubt, Lucado will name some of your personal fears in his book. Fear of one thing or another creeps into every conversation we have. Fear is easy to talk about, but confusing to overcome.<br /><br />Lucado points out that Jesus took human fear seriously and made it a priority to teach his disciples about fear. Christ's language throughout the Gospels is seasoned with phrases like "don't be afraid" and "take courage."<br /><br />He often told followers, "I tell you not to worry," "Do not fear," and "Don't let your hearts be troubled."<br /><br />Lucado points out that Jesus even told the crippled man brought to him by friends, "Take courage, son; your sins are forgiven."<br /><br />At first glance, this "encouragement" is confusing. The problem wasn't sin, it was paralysis. The problem was that the man couldn't meet his own needs because he lived on a mat.<br /><br />"Before Jesus healed the body (which he did), he treated the soul," writes Lucado. "To sin is to disregard God, ignore his teachings, deny his blessings," Lucado continues. "The sinner's life is me-focused, not God-focused."<br /><br />Lucado has chapters discussing your fear of insignificance, your fear of not pleasing God, your fear of running out of what you need, your fear of not protecting your kids, your fear of violence, your fear of death, your fear of global calamity and your fear of finding out that God may not be there.<br /><br />Overcoming fear takes a healthy dose of perspective. Lucado helps us see life from a different vantage point. Lucado emphasizes that we must walk through our fears with Christ. We can't take control of them in our own strength or with our own wisdom. Without a biblical view of our fear, we won't understand it and we won't apply a beneficial solution.<br /><br />Rehearsing our fear causes us to forget to rely on Jesus. We strive to provide for our own needs and security rather than trust God. The fortune we amass in this life is like Monopoly money, Lucado says. It's fake in God's economy. Fear causes us to invest in things that matter little.<br /><br />"Feed your fears, and your faith will starve," he writes. "Feed your faith, and your fears will."<br /><br />Lucado has fun with the disclaimers tagged onto the end of prescription drug advertisements on television.<br /><br />He lays out this satirical scenario of a lawyer reading the fine print to the inhabitant of a pregnant mother's belly: "Welcome to the post-umbilical cord world. Be advised, however, that human life has been known, in most cases, to result in death. Some individuals have reported experiences with lethal viruses, chemical agents and/or bloodthirsty terrorists. Birth can also result in fatal encounters with tsunamis, inebriated pilots, road rage, famine, nuclear disasters and/or PMS. Side effects of living include super viruses, heart disease and final exams. Human life is not recommended for anyone who cannot share a planet with evil despots or survive a flight on airplane food."<br /><br />"But it is in storms that [God] does his finest work, for it is in storms that he has our keenest attention," Lucado adds.<br /><br />Lucado says, "Everything will work out in the end. If it's not working out, it's not the end."<br /><br />"Fearless" comes with an excellent discussion guide to help readers work through issues privately or with others.<br /><br />We can all use some help working through our fears, and Lucado has given us an excellent tool to do so.<br /><br /> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://goodnewsfl.org/christian-news/fearless/">http://goodnewsfl.org/christian-news/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7579936715004024493" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_78070967" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78070967" />
    <a title="Lori" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2953227-lori"><img alt="Lori" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1258472828p2/2953227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78070967?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lori" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lori" href="/user/show/2953227-lori">Lori</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78070967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14438562289224543156">I have enjoyed many Max Lucado books, but I have to admit I am not a Max Lucado die-hard fan. For me many of his books began to run together and sound the same. I say that to tell you how much I loved Fearless by Max Lucado. I could not put the book down. Fear is something I struggle with, you name it I am sure I had some fear over it.<br/><br/>God makes it clear that if we as Christians are going to live a life of faith, we need to trust and step out into the unknown. Unfortunately to do that you need to</span>
  <span id="freeText14438562289224543156" style="display:none">I have enjoyed many Max Lucado books, but I have to admit I am not a Max Lucado die-hard fan. For me many of his books began to run together and sound the same. I say that to tell you how much I loved Fearless by Max Lucado. I could not put the book down. Fear is something I struggle with, you name it I am sure I had some fear over it.<br /><br />God makes it clear that if we as Christians are going to live a life of faith, we need to trust and step out into the unknown. Unfortunately to do that you need to turn over your fears and allow God to work through you. Satan likes to prey on our fears while making things seem impossible, even to God. In this well written, powerful book Max tackles fears all of us struggle with. Several of the topics covered are:<br /><br />Fear of not mattering.<br />Fear of disappointing God.<br />Fear of not protecting my kids.<br />Fear of violence.<br />Fear of death.<br />Fear that God may not be real.<br />Fear of coming out of my box.<br /><br />One of my favorite quotes in the book is when Max is retelling the story of the disciples out in a boat in rocky seas. Through this bible story we are reminded God is always with us, but it is not always easy sailing. "Getting on board with Christ can mean getting soaked with Christ. Disciples can expect rough seas and stout winds." Life may toss you around, but in the end you don't go under. What a powerful image of the Christian walk!<br /><br />Powerful stories and parables woven through out this book made the powerful God lessons dance off the page. This book is a book that offers encouragement, healing, and strength in dealing with the cancer of fear. If you are living your Christian walk out of your comfort zone, this is the perfect book to have on your bookshelf to read yearly.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14438562289224543156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_116869579" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/116869579" />
    <a title="Win Itmama" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4154886-win-itmama"><img alt="Win Itmama" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1281869686p2/4154886.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/116869579?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Win Itmama" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Win Itmama" href="/user/show/4154886-win-itmama">Win Itmama</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer116869579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14485561654729007234">“Imagine your life, wholly untouched by angst. What if faith, not fear, was your default reaction to threats? If you could hover a fear magnet over your heart and extract every last shaving of dread, insecurity, or doubt, what would remain? Envision a day, just one day, where you could trust more and fear less.”<br/><br/>I’ve never read a Christian book, better yet ANY religious book, besides the Bible. So when I read the words “Religion/Christian Life” as the category for Fearless by Max Lucado… I must a</span>
  <span id="freeText14485561654729007234" style="display:none">“Imagine your life, wholly untouched by angst. What if faith, not fear, was your default reaction to threats? If you could hover a fear magnet over your heart and extract every last shaving of dread, insecurity, or doubt, what would remain? Envision a day, just one day, where you could trust more and fear less.”<br /><br />I’ve never read a Christian book, better yet ANY religious book, besides the Bible. So when I read the words “Religion/Christian Life” as the category for Fearless by Max Lucado… I must admit I was a bit hesitant. But why? What was I afraid of? Something about the words “Imagine Your Life Without Fear” and the photo of a boy leaping into a body of water, started hitting my curiosity button. I had no clue what I was in for – but I can say I felt really open to exploring. After reading Fearless I have a better outlook on what fear is, what it leads to and how to replace fear with faith. Everyday, we hold back in life because of fear. Fearing our children may get hurt playing outside or cancelling a flight in fear of crashing. Max Lucado explains how our everyday fears can lead to the worse if we allow them to eat us up. I’d highly recommend this book to everyone. It’s like splashing cold water on your face, truly a wakeup.<br /><br />Disclosure of Material Connection: I received this book free from Thomas Nelson Publishers as part of their BookSneeze.com book review bloggers program. I was not required to write a positive review. The opinions I have expressed are my own. I am disclosing this in accordance with the Federal Trade Commission’s 16 CFR, Part 255 : “Guides Concerning the Use of Endorsements and Testimonials in Advertising.”</span>

<div id="review_131630058" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/131630058" />
    <a title="Sidney W." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4561157-sidney-w"><img alt="Sidney W." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1290202723p2/4561157.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/131630058?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sidney W." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sidney W." href="/user/show/4561157-sidney-w">Sidney W.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4561157-sidney-w?shelf=non-fiction-inspirational">non-fiction-inspirational</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer131630058" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7648594527501019124">I went to the Writers' League of Texas Agents Conference last month. At one of the sessions I heard about how bloggers can get free books from publishers in return for reviews. One publisher mentioned in particular was Thomas Nelson. I knew this company published Christian books so I contacted them and was approved to do reviews. <br/><br/>When asked, I specified Christian Fiction because that would fit best with The Christian Bookmobile. However, when I checked in to request a book, the only one availabl</span>
  <span id="freeText7648594527501019124" style="display:none">I went to the Writers' League of Texas Agents Conference last month. At one of the sessions I heard about how bloggers can get free books from publishers in return for reviews. One publisher mentioned in particular was Thomas Nelson. I knew this company published Christian books so I contacted them and was approved to do reviews. <br /><br />When asked, I specified Christian Fiction because that would fit best with The Christian Bookmobile. However, when I checked in to request a book, the only one available to me was Fearless by Max Lucado, a non-fiction book. <br /><br />While waiting for the book to be delivered, I read the sample chapters provided online (Chapters 1 and 9) and, based on what I read, found a solution to a problem I was experiencing in my life. I didn't think until later that perhaps this was another example of how God helps us in mysterious ways. <br /><br />I have much to be thankful for in my life, but two recent negative incidents, both out of my control, completely overshadowed the positives. As I read Fearless, I realized I was feeling fear. Lucado writes, "...fear is unwilling to share the heart with happiness. Happiness complies and leaves." Aha, that was what was happening to me. <br /><br />Continuing to read, I found the solution. "What if faith, not fear was your default reaction to threats?" Then, I understood. At that moment, my fear and feelings of being out of control went away. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7648594527501019124" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/69795045?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna" href="/user/show/2291555-donna">Donna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2291555-donna?shelf=books-read-in-2009">books-read-in-2009</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer69795045" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2597323066364419571"> Faith over fear. "Fearless," by Max Lucado, offers practical solutions and Scripture to life's challenges. What is fear? It is really a lack of the ability to control the outcome to a situation. This wonderful book looks at our fears over children, money, the unknown, life, and death. He lists Scripture with each situation to help underscore the fact that God is with us ALL the time. We aren't alone and God's peace can alleviate our fear. Is it really that easy? -with practice leaning on the ev</span>
  <span id="freeText2597323066364419571" style="display:none"> Faith over fear. "Fearless," by Max Lucado, offers practical solutions and Scripture to life's challenges. What is fear? It is really a lack of the ability to control the outcome to a situation. This wonderful book looks at our fears over children, money, the unknown, life, and death. He lists Scripture with each situation to help underscore the fact that God is with us ALL the time. We aren't alone and God's peace can alleviate our fear. Is it really that easy? -with practice leaning on the everlasting arms it can be. Can anyone live a fearless life? Yes! With stories, some humorous, and Biblical suggestions Max Lucado lays out a roadmap to follow.<br /><br /> I really enjoyed this book. It helped me look practically at the fears that surround me and offered help and hope that they can be overcome. Had I already heard the message? Did I know the Scriptures? Yes. But sometimes we need a reminder to get us back on track. God ALWAYS sends messages our way to help us live our lives fully and without fear. But, we let things get in the way of His comfort and guidance. I enjoyed Mr. Lucado's use of humor to bring home his points. I loved the Scriptures he used, and found great comfort in them. This is definitely a book to keep on your shelf as a constant reminder and tool to help you lead a "Fearless" life.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2597323066364419571" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7545257-jessica?shelf=my-favorite-books">my-favorite-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer394124432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3714971845802962670">I really loved this book by Max Lucado. It was right up there with my other favorite of his, "Facing Your Giants."<br/><br/>This book, as you can guess by the title, is all about conquering fear. When I first picked it up, I thought it would be more of a generic, overall look at fear. Kind of like looking at everything overall and just evaluating fear itself and ways to overcome it. Instead, what I found was a very in-depth look at all the different kinds of fear, and doubt, that Christians face in today'</span>
  <span id="freeText3714971845802962670" style="display:none">I really loved this book by Max Lucado. It was right up there with my other favorite of his, "Facing Your Giants."<br /><br />This book, as you can guess by the title, is all about conquering fear. When I first picked it up, I thought it would be more of a generic, overall look at fear. Kind of like looking at everything overall and just evaluating fear itself and ways to overcome it. Instead, what I found was a very in-depth look at all the different kinds of fear, and doubt, that Christians face in today's society. There was everything from financial and world related fears such as war and violence to the very basic fears of bad health and disappointing God.<br /><br />Instead of a "how to conquer your fears" manual, this book pointed you to THE ONE whom we should always rely on. In true Max style, he reminds us that God is bigger than any fears and doubts we have. In reading this book, suddenly you are reminded just how puny your fears are and just how unlimited God is. And equally comforting came the emphasis that God was plenty capable of not only dealing with our fears about, well, everything and anything, but that He has the power to help us overcome them. <br /><br />This book was such an encouragement to read. It was a great reminder that, in Christ, we can overcome anything. Even our fears.<br /><br />I fully plan on putting it on my book wish list.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3714971845802962670" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText1964200573638117507" style="display:none">"I recommend Fearless to anyone who is tired of doom and gloom and ready to step out of fear once and for all."<br /><br />- Dave Ramsey, The Dave Ramsey Show<br /><br /><br />Imagine Your Life Without Fear<br /><br /><br />How would you like to live your life fearless? Great Bible principles outlines his wonderful illustrations of stories makes this an easy read for most, however it will also challenge hardcore Bible student.<br /><br />Max always using Jesus as the main attraction in his writing makes you ponder about the awesome person He is. This book will have you reading it again and again. This book is one that you will want to share with people that you come in contact with.<br /><br />Remember, Jesus has never left us and He will be coming back for us soon.<br /></span>

<div id="review_177825036" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/177825036" />
    <a title="Britni" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/389139-britni"><img alt="Britni" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598115687p2/389139.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/177825036?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Britni" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Britni" href="/user/show/389139-britni">Britni</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer177825036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14308173291952114378">Fearless is about how to deal with and replace all sorts of fears with faith. The book is being released today so it's written in an extremely scary time for many people. From the fear of not being liked, to fear of financial failure, to fear of being eaten by a shark, Lucado covers them all. And gives suggestions for ways to overcome these fears by trusting in God and doing all we can do and realizing He is the only one who can really control everything.<br/><br/>I really enjoyed this book. There is some</span>
  <span id="freeText14308173291952114378" style="display:none">Fearless is about how to deal with and replace all sorts of fears with faith. The book is being released today so it's written in an extremely scary time for many people. From the fear of not being liked, to fear of financial failure, to fear of being eaten by a shark, Lucado covers them all. And gives suggestions for ways to overcome these fears by trusting in God and doing all we can do and realizing He is the only one who can really control everything.<br /><br />I really enjoyed this book. There is something for everyone in it regardless of what religion you follow or don't. Max Lucado's writing is filled with humor and everyday experiences from people he's met through his life, and this really helped his points hit home for me. Especially the chapter on not being liked and why does it really matter what other people think when God's the one who created you and he doesn't make mistakes. Again, if you've never read You Are Special, it's one of the best children's books out there. And this is another great book from Lucado, I'm glad I was given the chance to read it and hope that other people pick it up as soon as it hits the shelves today. Because you really don't have to fear anything but God. 5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14308173291952114378" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1254289665" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1254289665" />
    <a title="Katie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27247586-katie"><img alt="Katie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494793009p2/27247586.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1254289665?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie" href="/user/show/27247586-katie">Katie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1254289665" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5723769745005641276">I feel like this book is probably great for people who have a few, vague fears from time to time. But if you're looking for something to help you overcome deep-seeded fears and trust problems, you are definitely in the wrong place. <br/><br/>Basically, Fearless addressed approximately ten different fears you might have in a very shallow way. Using text from the Bible of Jesus telling people (usually the disciples) not to be afraid, Max Lucado elaborated on why being afraid is unbiblical, usually through a</span>
  <span id="freeText5723769745005641276" style="display:none">I feel like this book is probably great for people who have a few, vague fears from time to time. But if you're looking for something to help you overcome deep-seeded fears and trust problems, you are definitely in the wrong place. <br /><br />Basically, Fearless addressed approximately ten different fears you might have in a very shallow way. Using text from the Bible of Jesus telling people (usually the disciples) not to be afraid, Max Lucado elaborated on why being afraid is unbiblical, usually through anecdotes. But he rarely addressed HOW to be unafraid. If all you need to know to quench your fears is that God's got your back, this book gives you plenty of positive feedback. But if you've already read the Bible, understand how God looks after you, and STILL have trouble with fear, this shallow look at the Bible is going to seem just that, shallow. If you feel anxious about money from time to time, this book is going to help you understand how to deal with that. If you've been jobless for three years and are very quickly facing homelessness, this book probably isn't going to have anything to say that you haven't already told yourself a million times before.<br /><br />My suggestion: Instead of reading this book read the Bible and go to Sunday School class. You'll probably get more out of it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5723769745005641276" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/237531930?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth" href="/user/show/5059710-elizabeth">Elizabeth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5059710-elizabeth?shelf=christian">christian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5059710-elizabeth?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5059710-elizabeth?shelf=faith">faith</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer237531930" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8533157038430330508">This book provides an answer for the worries of daily life, and Max Lucado writes with a distinctive voice: funny in some places, serious in others, and comforting throughout. I laughed out loud in a few places, and I was delighted as his ability to take an austere topic, specifically a Bible passage, and relay it with both respect and hilarity.<br/><br/>My only complaint is that although the book addresses aspects of secular life that may cause fear, such as deaths, alcohol addictions, financial struggle</span>
  <span id="freeText8533157038430330508" style="display:none">This book provides an answer for the worries of daily life, and Max Lucado writes with a distinctive voice: funny in some places, serious in others, and comforting throughout. I laughed out loud in a few places, and I was delighted as his ability to take an austere topic, specifically a Bible passage, and relay it with both respect and hilarity.<br /><br />My only complaint is that although the book addresses aspects of secular life that may cause fear, such as deaths, alcohol addictions, financial struggles, wars, illnesses, and unemployment, he fails to address fears that come from faith life. In fact, he tends to write the issue off entirely, saying that if you aren't sure that you have accepted God, then you haven't. I disagree, as I think that it's much more complicated than that. However, in pretty much all aspects of life except this one, this book can be (and is) a great source of comfort.<br /><br />It takes only a few minutes to read this book, and Lucado draws on his own family history, on a Biblical parable, and on several verses of comfort from the Old and New Testaments. Well worth the read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8533157038430330508" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10148840525960855740"><br/>From constant worrying to losing a child and into an acrobatic flight with training for use of an ejector seat, Max Lucado writes with a deep comprehension of all fears humans face. He has an excellent grasp of psychology, uses vivid analogies and just the right level of humour. This is only the third book I have given a five star rating. It’s what I save my five stars for. Ican’t recommend this bookhighly enough. Readit. Enjoy it. And learn. My next Max Lucado bookis ready and waiting.<br/></span>

    <a title="Brett" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71969719-brett"><img alt="Brett" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2525616159?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brett" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brett" href="/user/show/71969719-brett">Brett</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2525616159" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18246320270810998756">Living in a broken world with imperfect people its no wonder people are filled with such anxiety and fear. Fear robs us of our wonder of creation and the joy of exploring it. Fear keeps us from truly living. In "Fearless" Max Lucado tackles 14 different topics that we fear. While some of these topics ex: "Fear of violence" , "Fear of Coming Winter", "Fear of Worst Case Scenario" could be combined into one category; Max Lucado does explore fears that are not only common but perhaps are prevalent.</span>
  <span id="freeText18246320270810998756" style="display:none">Living in a broken world with imperfect people its no wonder people are filled with such anxiety and fear. Fear robs us of our wonder of creation and the joy of exploring it. Fear keeps us from truly living. In "Fearless" Max Lucado tackles 14 different topics that we fear. While some of these topics ex: "Fear of violence" , "Fear of Coming Winter", "Fear of Worst Case Scenario" could be combined into one category; Max Lucado does explore fears that are not only common but perhaps are prevalent. I enjoy the practical style in which Lucado writes, his information and help is very welcoming and useful. Definitely a good and easy read. While Fearless isn't theologically deep, it is very needed and completely relevant. </span>

<div id="review_70173652" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/70173652" />
    <a title="Debbie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1709540-debbie"><img alt="Debbie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1237914398p2/1709540.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/70173652?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie" href="/user/show/1709540-debbie">Debbie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1709540-debbie?shelf=christian">christian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1709540-debbie?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer70173652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18150368091659063604">This excellent and timely book is God-focused, Scripture-focused, and deepens the reader's understanding of God. It covers why we fear and how to be released from the fear of not mattering, of disappointing God, of running out of time, of not being able to protect your kids, of challenges that might overwhelm you, of worst-case scenarios happening, of violence, of not being able to provide for your family, of an unknown future, of death, that maybe God isn't real after all, of global calamity, a</span>
  <span id="freeText18150368091659063604" style="display:none">This excellent and timely book is God-focused, Scripture-focused, and deepens the reader's understanding of God. It covers why we fear and how to be released from the fear of not mattering, of disappointing God, of running out of time, of not being able to protect your kids, of challenges that might overwhelm you, of worst-case scenarios happening, of violence, of not being able to provide for your family, of an unknown future, of death, that maybe God isn't real after all, of global calamity, and of God doing something you don't want him to. There's also a discussion guide at the back of the book.<br /><br />With so many people telling us that we need to fear (not to mention give them money to make the fearsome thing go away), sometimes it's hard to keep our focus on Christ. As Christians, we know that we shouldn't worry, yet we often do...and then feel guilty about it. This book helps readers get their focus right and find lasting peace in the deep-down assurance that God really is in control, does care about us, and will fulfill his promises.<br /><br />Even if you decide not to buy this book, please still take the time to read the first chapter. It's a good reminder even if you already know these truths, and it's vital for those who don't know but who want peace and assurance about the present and future.<br /><br /><br />Max Lucado also wrote a companion booklet, "Imagine Your Life Without Fear." It contains the first chapter of the "Fearless" book (which is an excellent chapter) plus a short, outreach chapter and a chapter containing Bible verses pertaining to all the fears covered in "Fearless." If you can't afford to buy "Fearless" for all your friends, this booklet is an excellent alternative.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18150368091659063604" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_67251444" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/67251444" />
    <a title="Michael Brown" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2233730-michael-brown"><img alt="Michael Brown" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1269091271p2/2233730.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/67251444?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Brown" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Brown" href="/user/show/2233730-michael-brown">Michael Brown</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer67251444" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14669460645109530634">Fearless by Max Lucado is actually a really good book. The subtitle on the cover is "Imagine your life without fear. I have to admit I used to read everything that Max put out back in the late 90's but after a while he seemed a little too light for me. And then I was offered a copy of this book to review - so for the first time in years I sat down to read a book by Max. <br/><br/>I was pleasantly surprised; this book has something for everyone in it. There is at least one chapter which will speak to you. </span>
  <span id="freeText14669460645109530634" style="display:none">Fearless by Max Lucado is actually a really good book. The subtitle on the cover is "Imagine your life without fear. I have to admit I used to read everything that Max put out back in the late 90's but after a while he seemed a little too light for me. And then I was offered a copy of this book to review - so for the first time in years I sat down to read a book by Max. <br /><br />I was pleasantly surprised; this book has something for everyone in it. There is at least one chapter which will speak to you. Be it: "The fear of: Not Mattering, Disappointing God, Running Out or Away, Not Protecting Your Kids, Overwhelming Challenges, Worst Case Scenarios, Violence, Coming Winter, Life's Final Moments, What's Next, That God Is Not There, Global Calamity, or The Fear of Getting Out Of Your Box. Max helps you work through it. It will not be an easy road but it is well worth the journey. <br /><br />So, if you're looking for a good book on dealing with fear - this is a great book to read. It truly has something for everyone. And it is not to light and not to heavy - it's just right. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14669460645109530634" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16331975946246409096">Short review: The basic format was a chapter for a specific type of fear. Then Lucado would talk about why we should not fear this particular thing. In general I think it was ok, but it was repetitive and there were a few chapters where I strongly disagreed. <br/><br/>I agree that the topic is relevant, I know many people that seem to fear everything. Lucado was biblical and gave good relevant stories to illustrate his point, but the point was basically the same with every chapter that you just need to tr</span>
  <span id="freeText16331975946246409096" style="display:none">Short review: The basic format was a chapter for a specific type of fear. Then Lucado would talk about why we should not fear this particular thing. In general I think it was ok, but it was repetitive and there were a few chapters where I strongly disagreed. <br /><br />I agree that the topic is relevant, I know many people that seem to fear everything. Lucado was biblical and gave good relevant stories to illustrate his point, but the point was basically the same with every chapter that you just need to trust God more.<br /><br />There are other books on fear that I think are better so I would not particularly recommend this one. A better book is Rhett Smith's The Anxious Christian (my review <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bookwi.se/anxious-christian/">http://bookwi.se/anxious-christian/</a> )<br /><br />I posted a longer review on my blog at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bookwi.se/fearless-by-max-lucado/">http://bookwi.se/fearless-by-max-lucado/</a><br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NmshLmnuuKOl4M3lbSDFX6LT3+OL1iGPqVlthBq56xKvND86k8qfF8hBVZQ/6F/syYuVhIYX8tgFhWfvf1AClA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/yxB0J5tDyNF/ZXWBNgECy7WRm8thGymht2W7qBxrAlmc1/EZEkolyhcDadWEJ64RY4MCCBFv/EqAZyFxZhFjw==')})
  }

Gordon alone survived. And forgave. He said of the bombers, \' I have lost my daughter, but I bear no grudge . . . I shall pray, tonight and every night, that God will forgive them.\' His words caught the media\'s ears  and out of one man\'s grief, the world got a glimpse of grace. Grace is the church\'s great distinctive. It\'s the one thing the world cannot duplicate, and the one thing it craves above all else  for only grace can bring hope and transformation to a jaded world. In What\'s So Amazing About Grace? award-winning author Philip Yancey explores grace at street level. If grace is God\'s love for the undeserving, he asks, then what does it look like in action? And if Christians are its sole dispensers, then how are we doing at lavishing grace on a world that knows far more of cruelty and unforgiveness than it does of mercy? Yancey sets grace in the midst of life\'s stark images, tests its mettle against horrific \'ungrace.\' Can grace survive in the midst of such atrocities as the Nazi holocaust? Can it triumph over the brutality of the Ku Klux Klan? Should any grace at all be shown to the likes of Jeffrey Dahmer, who killed and cannibalized seventeen young men? Grace does not excuse sin, says Yancey, but it treasures the sinner. True grace is shocking, scandalous. It shakes our conventions with its insistence on getting close to sinners and touching them with mercy and hope. It forgives the unfaithful spouse, the racist, the child abuser. It loves today\'s AIDS-ridden addict as much as the tax collector of Jesus\' day. In his most personal and provocative book ever, Yancey offers compelling, true portraits of grace\'s life-changing power. He searches for its presence in his own life and in the church. He asks, How can Christians contend graciously with moral issues that threaten all they hold dear?
